These\n153: /// requirements are then verified and proved by the closure's\n154: /// creating function. This struct encodes those requirements.\n155: ///\n156: /// The requirements are listed as being between various `RegionVid`. The 0th\n157: /// region refers to `'static`; subsequent region vids refer to the free\n158: /// regions that appear in the closure (or coroutine's) type, in order of\n159: /// appearance. (This numbering is actually defined by the `UniversalRegions`\n160: /// struct in the NLL region checker. See for example\n161: /// `UniversalRegions::closure_mapping`.) Note the free regions in the\n162: /// closure's signature and captures are erased.\n163: ///\n164: /// Example: If type check produces a closure with the closure args:\n165: ///\n166: /// ```text\n167: /// ClosureArgs = [\n168: ///     'a,                                         // From the parent.\n169: ///     'b,\n170: ///     i8,                                         // the \"closure kind\"\n171: ///     for<'x> fn(&'<erased> &'x u32) -> &'x u32,  // the \"closure signature\"\n172: ///     &'<erased> String,                          // some upvar\n173: /// ]\n174: /// ```\n175: ///\n176: /// We would \"renumber\" each free region to a unique vid, as follows:\n177: ///\n178: /// ```text\n179: /// ClosureArgs = [\n180: ///     '1,                                         // From the parent.\n181: ///     '2,\n182: ///     i8,                                         // the \"closure kind\"\n183: ///     for<'x> fn(&'3 &'x u32) -> &'x u32,         // the \"closure signature\"\n184: ///     &'4 String,                                 // some upvar\n185: /// ]\n186: /// ```\n187: ///\n188: /// Now the code might impose a requirement like `'1: '2`. When an\n189: /// instance of the closure is created, the corresponding free regions\n190: /// can be extracted from its type and constrained to have the given\n191: /// outlives relationship.\n192: #[derive(Clone, Debug)]\n193: pub struct ClosureRegionRequirements<'tcx> {\n194:     /// The number of external regions defined on the closure. I> !TypeFoldable<I> for ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx> {}\n254: \n255: impl<'tcx> ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx> {\n256:     /// All regions of `ty` must be of kind `ReVar` and must represent\n257:     /// universal regions *external* to the closure.\n258:     pub fn bind(tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>, ty: Ty<'tcx>) -> Self {\n259:         let inner = fold_regions(tcx, ty, |r, depth| match r.kind() {\n260: // a user-declared local. MirBorrowckCtxt<'a, '_, 'tcx> {\n787:     fn visit_after_early_statement_effect(\n788:         &mut self,\n789:         _analysis: &Borrowck<'a, 'tcx>,\n790:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n791:                self.consume_rvalue(location, (rhs, span), state);\n802: \n803:                 self.mutate_place(location, (*lhs, span), Shallow(None), state);\n804:             }\n805:             StatementKind::FakeRead(box (_, place)) => {\n806:                 // Read for match doesn't access any memory and is used to\n807:                 // assert that a place is safe and live. So we don't have to\n808:                 // do any checks here.\n809:                 //\n810:                 // FIXME: Remove check that the place is initialized. StatementKind::Intrinsic(box kind) => match kind {\n824:                 NonDivergingIntrinsic::Assume(op) => {\n825:                     self.consume_operand(location, (op, span), state);\n826: }\n917:             TerminatorKind::TailCall { func, args, fn_span: _ } => {\n918:                 self.consume_operand(loc, (func, span), state);\n919:                 for arg in args {\n920:                     self.consume_operand(loc, (&arg.node, arg.span), state);\n921:                 }\n922:             }\n923:             TerminatorKind::Assert { cond, expected: _, msg, target: _, unwind: _ } => {\n924:                 self.consume_operand(loc, (cond, span), state);\n925:                 if let AssertKind::BoundsCheck { len, index } = &**msg {\n926:                     self.consume_operand(loc, (len, span), state);\n927:                     self.consume_operand(loc, (index, span), state);\n928:                 }\n929:             }\n930: \n931:             TerminatorKind::Yield { value, resume: _, resume_arg, drop: _ } => {\n932:                 self.consume_operand(loc, (value, span), state);\n933:                 self.mutate_place(loc, (*resume_arg, span), Deep, state);\n934:             }\n935: \n936:             TerminatorKind::InlineAsm {\n937:                 asm_macro: _,\n938:                 template: _,\n939:                 operands,\n940:                 options: _,\n941:                 line_spans: _,\n942:                 targets: _,\n943:                 unwind: _,\n944:             } => {\n945:                 for op in operands {\n946:                     match op {\n947:                         InlineAsmOperand::In { reg: _, value } => {\n948:                             self.consume_operand(loc, (value, span), state);\n949:                         }\n950:                         InlineAsmOperand::Out { reg: _, late: _, place, .. } => {\n951:                             if let Some(place) = place {\n952:                                 self.mutate_place(loc, (*place, span), Shallow(None), state);\n953:                             }\n954:                         }\n955:                         InlineAsmOperand::InOut { reg: _, late: _, in_value, out_place } => {\n956:                             self.consume_operand(loc, (in_value, span), state);\n957:                             if let &Some(out_place) = out_place {\n958:                                 self.mutate_place(loc, (out_place, span), Shallow(None), state);\n959:                             }\n960:                         }\n961:                         InlineAsmOperand::Const { value: _ }\n962:                         | InlineAsmOperand::SymFn { value: _ }\n963:                         | InlineAsmOperand::SymStatic { def_id: _ }\n964:                         | InlineAsmOperand::Label { target_index: _ } => {}\n965:                     }\n966:                 }\n967:             }\n968: \n969:             TerminatorKind::Goto { target: _ }\n970:             | TerminatorKind::UnwindTerminate(_)\n971:             | TerminatorKind::Unreachable\n972:             | TerminatorKind::UnwindResume\n973:             | TerminatorKind::Return\n974:             | TerminatorKind::CoroutineDrop\n975:             | TerminatorKind::FalseEdge { real_target: _, imaginary_target: _ }\n976:             | TerminatorKind::FalseUnwind { real_target: _, unwind: _ } => {\n977:                 // no data used, thus irrelevant to borrowck\n978:             }\n979:         }\n980:     }\n981: \n982:     fn visit_after_primary_terminator_effect(\n983:         &mut self,\n984:         _analysis: &Borrowck<'a, 'tcx>,\n985:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n986:         term: &Terminator<'tcx>,\n987:         loc: Location,\n988:     ) {\n989:         let span = term.source_info.span;\n990: \n991:         match term.kind {\n992:             TerminatorKind::Yield { value: _, resume: _, resume_arg: _, drop: _ } => {\n993:                 if self.movable_coroutine {\n994:                     // Look for any active borrows to locals\n995:                     for i in state.borrows.iter() {\n996:                         let borrow = &self.borrow_set[i];\n997:                         self.check_for_local_borrow(borrow, span);\n998:                     }\n999:                 }\n1000:             }\n1001: \n1002:             TerminatorKind::UnwindResume\n1003:             | TerminatorKind::Return\n1004:             | TerminatorKind::TailCall { .. }\n1005:             | TerminatorKind::CoroutineDrop => {\n1006:                 match self.borrow_set.locals_state_at_exit() {\n1007:                     LocalsStateAtExit::AllAreInvalidated => {\n1008:                         // Returning from the function implicitly kills storage for all locals and statics.\n1009:                         // Often, the storage will already have been killed by an explicit\n1010:                         // StorageDead, but we don't always emit those (notably on unwind paths),\n1011:                         // so this \"extra check\" serves as a kind of backup.\n1012:                         for i in state.borrows.iter() {\n1013:                             let borrow = &self.borrow_set[i];\n1014:                             self.check_for_invalidation_at_exit(loc, borrow, span);\n1015:                         }\n1016:                     }\n1017:                     // If we do not implicitly invalidate all locals on exit,\n1018:                     // we check for conflicts when dropping or moving this local.\n1019:                     LocalsStateAtExit::SomeAreInvalidated { has_storage_dead_or_moved: _ } => {}\n1020:                 }\n1021:             }\n1022: \n1023:             TerminatorKind::UnwindTerminate(_)\n1024:             | TerminatorKind::Assert { .. }\n1025:             | TerminatorKind::Call { .. }\n1026:             | TerminatorKind::Drop { .. }\n1027:             | TerminatorKind::FalseEdge { real_target: _, imaginary_target: _ }\n1028:             | TerminatorKind::FalseUnwind { real_target: _, unwind: _ }\n1029:             | TerminatorKind::Goto { .. }\n1030:             | TerminatorKind::SwitchInt { .. }\n1031:             | TerminatorKind::Unreachable\n1032:             | TerminatorKind::InlineAsm { .. } => {}\n1033:         }\n1034:     }\n1035: }\n1036: \n1037: use self::AccessDepth::{Deep, Shallow};\n1038: use self::ReadOrWrite::{Activation, Read, Reservation, Write};\n1039: \n1040: #[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Debug)]\n1041: enum ArtificialField {\n1042:     ArrayLength,\n1043:     FakeBorrow,\n1044: }\n1045: \n1046: #[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Debug)]\n1047: enum AccessDepth {\n1048:     /// From the RFC: \"A *shallow* access means that the immediate\n1049:     /// fields reached at P are accessed, but references or pointers\n1050:     /// found within are not dereferenced. Right now, the only access\n1051:     /// that is shallow is an assignment like `x = ...;`, which would\n1052:     /// be a *shallow write* of `x`.\"\n1053:     Shallow(Option<ArtificialField>),\n1054: \n1055:     /// From the RFC: \"A *deep* access means that all data reachable\n1056:     /// through the given place may be invalidated or accesses by\n1057:     /// this action.\"\n1058:     Deep,\n1059: \n1060:     /// Access is Deep only when there is a Drop implementation that\n1061:     /// can reach the data behind the reference.\n1062:     Drop,\n1063: }\n1064: \n1065: /// Kind of access to a value: read or write\n1066: /// (For informational purposes only)\n1067: #[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Debug)]\n1068: enum ReadOrWrite {\n1069:     /// From the RFC: \"A *read* means that the existing data may be\n1070:     /// read, but will not be changed.\"\n1071:     Read(ReadKind),\n1072: \n1073:     /// From the RFC: \"A *write* means that the data may be mutated to\n1074:     /// new values or otherwise invalidated (for example, it could be\n1075:     /// de-initialized, as in a move operation).\n1076:     Write(WriteKind),\n1077: \n1078:     /// For two-phase borrows, we distinguish a reservation (which is treated\n1079:     /// like a Read) from an activation (which is treated like a write), and\n1080:     /// each of those is furthermore distinguished from Reads/Writes above.\n1081:     Reservation(WriteKind),\n1082:     Activation(WriteKind, BorrowIndex),\n1083: }\n1084: \n1085: /// Kind of read access to a value\n1086: /// (For informational purposes only)\n1087: #[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Debug)]\n1088: enum ReadKind {\n1089:     Borrow(BorrowKind),\n1090:     Copy,\n1091: }\n1092: \n1093: /// Kind of write access to a value\n1094: /// (For informational purposes only)\n1095: #[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Debug)]\n1096: enum WriteKind {\n1097:     StorageDeadOrDrop,\n1098:     Replace,\n1099:     MutableBorrow(BorrowKind),\n1100:     Mutate,\n1101:     Move,\n1102: }\n1103: \n1104: /// When checking permissions for a place access, this flag is used to indicate that an immutable\n1105: /// local place can be mutated.\n1106: //\n1107: // FIXME: @nikomatsakis suggested that this flag could be removed with the following modifications:\n1108: // {\n1122:     Borrow,\n1123:     MatchOn,\n1124:     Use,\n1125:     Assignment,\n1126:     PartialAssignment,\n1127: }\n1128: \n1129: #[derive(Debug)]\n1130: struct RootPlace<'tcx> {\n1131: {\n1137:     fn as_noun(self) -> &'static str {\n1138:         match self {\n1139:             InitializationRequiringAction::Borrow => \"borrow\",\n1140:      }\n1370:             },\n1371:         );\n1372: \n1373:         error_reported\n1374:     }\n1375: \n1376:     /// Through #123739, `BackwardIncompatibleDropHint`s (BIDs) are introduced.\n1377:     /// We would like to emit lints whether borrow checking fails at these future drop locations.\n1378:     #[instrument(level = \"debug\", skip(self, state))]\n1379:     fn                 RawPtrKind::FakeForPtrMetadata => {\n1507:                         (Shallow(Some(ArtificialField::ArrayLength)), Read(ReadKind::Copy))\n1508:                     }\n1509:                 };\n1510: \n1511:                 self.access_place(\n1512:                     location,\n1513:                     (place, span),\n1514:                     access_kind,\n1515:                     LocalMutationIsAllowed::No,\n1516:                     state,\n1517:                 );\n1518: \n1519:                 self.check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved(\n1520:                     location,\n1521:                     InitializationRequiringAction::Borrow,\n1522:                     (place.as_ref(), span),\n1523:                     state,\n1524:                 );\n1525:             }\n1526: \n1527:             Rvalue::ThreadLocalRef(_) => {}\n1528: \n1529:             Rvalue::Use(operand)\n1530:             | Rvalue::Repeat(operand, _)\n1531:             | Rvalue::UnaryOp(_ /*un_op*/, operand)\n1532:             | Rvalue::Cast(_ /*cast_kind*/, operand, _ /*ty*/)\n1533:             | Rvalue::ShallowInitBox(operand, _ /*ty*/) => {\n1534:                 self.consume_operand(location, (operand, span), state)\n1535:             }\n1536: \n1537:             &Rvalue::Discriminant(place) => {\n1538:                 let af = match *rvalue {\n1539:                     Rvalue::Discriminant(..) => None,\n1540:                     _ => unreachable!(),\n1541:                 };\n1542:                 self.access_place(\n1543:                     location,\n1544:                     (place, span),\n1545:                     (Shallow(af), Read(ReadKind::Copy)),\n1546:                     LocalMutationIsAllowed::No,\n1547:                     state,\n1548:                 );\n1549:                 self.check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved(\n1550:                     location,\n1551:                     InitializationRequiringAction::Use,\n1552:                     (place.as_ref(), span),\n1553:                     state,\n1554:                 );\n1555:             }\n1556: \n1557:             Rvalue::BinaryOp(_bin_op, box (operand1, operand2)) => {\n1558:                 self.consume_operand(location, (operand1, span), state);\n1559:                 self.consume_operand(location, (operand2, span), state);\n1560:             }\n1561: \n1562:             Rvalue::NullaryOp(_op) => {\n1563:                 // nullary ops take no dynamic input; no borrowck effect.\n1564:             }\n1565: \n1566:             Rvalue::Aggregate(aggregate_kind, operands) => {\n1567:                 // We need to report back the list of mutable upvars that were\n1568:                 // moved into the closure and subsequently used by the closure,\n1569:                 // in order to populate our used_mut set.\n1570:                 match **aggregate_kind {\n1571:                     AggregateKind::Closure(def_id, _)\n1572:                     | AggregateKind::CoroutineClosure(def_id, _)\n1573:                     | AggregateKind::Coroutine(def_id, _) => {\n1574:                         let def_id = def_id.expect_local();\n1575:                         let used_mut_upvars = self.root_cx.used_mut_upvars(def_id);\n1576:                         debug!(\"{:?} used_mut_upvars={:?}\", def_id, used_mut_upvars);\n1577:                         // FIXME: We're cloning the `SmallVec` here to avoid borrowing `root_cx`\n1578:                         // when calling `propagate_closure_used_mut_upvar`. This should ideally\n1579:                         // be unnecessary.\n1580:                         for field in used_mut_upvars.clone() {\n1581:                             self.propagate_closure_used_mut_upvar(&operands[field]);\n1582:                         }\n1583:                     }\n1584:                     AggregateKind::Adt(..)\n1585:                     | AggregateKind::Array(..)\n1586:                     | AggregateKind::Tuple { .. }\n1587:                     | AggregateKind::RawPtr(..) => (),\n1588:                 }\n1589: \n1590:                 for operand in operands {\n1591:                     self.consume_operand(location, (operand, span), state);\n1592:                 }\n1593:             }\n1594: \n1595:             Rvalue::WrapUnsafeBinder(op, _) => {\n1596:                 self.consume_operand(location, (op, span), state);\n1597:             }\n1598: \n1599:             Rvalue::CopyForDeref(_) => bug!(\"`CopyForDeref` in borrowck\"),\n1600:         }\n1601:     }\n1602: \n1603:     fn propagate_closure_used_mut_upvar(&mut self, operand: &Operand<'tcx>) {\n1604:         let propagate_closure_used_mut_place = |this: &mut Self, place: Place<'tcx>| {\n1605:             // We have three possibilities here:\n1606:             // a. We are modifying something through a mut-ref\n1607:             // b. We are modifying something that is local to our parent\n1608:             // c. Current body is a nested closure, and we are modifying path starting from\n1609:             //    a Place captured by our parent closure.\n1610: \n1611:             // Handle (c), the path being modified is exactly the path captured by our parent\n1612:             if let Some(field) = this.is_upvar_field_projection(place.as_ref()) {\n1613:                 this.used_mut_upvars.push(field);\n1614:                 return;\n1615:             }\n1616: \n1617:             for (place_ref, proj) in place.iter_projections().rev() {\n1618:                 // Handle (a)\n1619:                 if proj == ProjectionElem::Deref {\n1620:                     match place_ref.ty(this.body(), this.infcx.tcx).ty.kind() {\n1621:                         // We aren't modifying a variable directly\n1622:                         ty::Ref(_, _, hir::Mutability::Mut) => return,\n1623: \n1624:                         _ => {}\n1625:                     }\n1626:                 }\n1627: \n1628:                 // Handle (c)\n1629:                 if let Some(field) = this.is_upvar_field_projection(place_ref) {\n1630:                     this.used_mut_upvars.push(field);\n1631:                     return;\n1632:                 }\n1633:             }\n1634: \n1635:             // Handle(b)\n1636:             this.used_mut.insert(place.local);\n1637:         };\n1638: \n1639:         // This relies on the current way that by-value\n1640:         // captures of a closure are copied/moved directly\n1641:         // when generating MIR.\n1642:         match *operand {\n1643:             Operand::Move(place) | Operand::Copy(place) => {\n1644:                 match place.as_local() {\n1645:                     Some(local) if !self.body.local_decls[local].is_user_variable() => {\n1646:                         if self.body.local_decls[local].ty.is_mutable_ptr() {\n1647:                             // The variable will be marked as mutable by the borrow.\n1648:                             return;\n1649:                         }\n1650:                         // This is an edge case where we have a `move` closure\n1651:                         // inside a non-move closure, and the inner closure\n1652:                         // contains a mutation:\n1653:                         //\n1654:                         // let mut i = 0;\n1655:                         // || { move || { i += 1; }; };\n1656:                         //\n1657:                         // In this case our usual strategy of assuming that the\n1658:                         // variable will be captured by mutable reference is\n1659:                         // wrong, since `i` can be copied into the inner\n1660:                         // closure from a shared reference.\n1661:                         //\n1662:                         // As such we have to search for the local that this\n1663:                         // capture comes from and mark it as being used as mut.\n1664: \n1665:                         let Some(temp_mpi) = self.move_data.rev_lookup.find_local(local) else {\n1666:                             bug!(\"temporary should be tracked\");\n1667:                         };\n1668:                         let init = if let [init_index] = *self.move_data.init_path_map[temp_mpi] {\n1669:                             &self.move_data.inits[init_index]\n1670:                         } else {\n1671:                             bug!(\"temporary should be initialized exactly once\")\n1672:                         };\n1673: \n1674:                         let InitLocation::Statement(loc) = init.location else {\n1675:                             bug!(\"temporary initialized in arguments\")\n1676:                         };\n1677: \n1678:                         let body = self.body;\n1679:                         let bbd = &body[loc.block];\n1680:                         let stmt = &bbd.statements[loc.statement_index];\n1681:                         debug!(\"temporary assigned in: stmt={:?}\", stmt);\n1682: \n1683:                         match stmt.kind {\n1684:                             StatementKind::Assign(box (\n1685:                                 _,\n1686:                                 Rvalue::Ref(_, _, source)\n1687:                                 | Rvalue::Use(Operand::Copy(source) | Operand::Move(source)),\n1688:                             )) => {\n1689:                                 propagate_closure_used_mut_place(self, source);\n1690:                             }\n1691:                             _ => {\n1692:                                 bug!(\n1693:                                     \"closures should only capture user variables \\\n1694:                                  or references to user variables\"\n1695:                                 );\n1696:                             }\n1697:                         }\n1698:                     }\n1699:                     _ => propagate_closure_used_mut_place(self, place),\n1700:                 }\n1701:             }\n1702:             Operand::Constant(..) => {}\n1703:         }\n1704:     }\n1705: \n1706:     fn consume_operand(\n1707:         &mut self,\n1708:         location: Location,\n1709:         (operand, span): (&Operand<'tcx>, Span),\n1710:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n1711:     ) {\n1712:         match *operand {\n1713:             Operand::Copy(place) => {\n1714:                 // copy of place: check if this is \"copy of frozen path\"\n1715:                 // (FIXME: see check_loans.rs)\n1716:                 self.access_place(\n1717:                     location,\n1718:                     (place, span),\n1719:                     (Deep, Read(ReadKind::Copy)),\n1720:                     LocalMutationIsAllowed::No,\n1721:                     state,\n1722:                 );\n1723: \n1724:                 // Finally, InitializationRequiringAction::Use,\n1728:                     (place.as_ref(), span),\n1729:                     state,\n1730:                 );\n1731:             }\n1732:             Operand::Move(place) => {\n1733:                 // Check if moving from this place makes sense.\n1734:                 self.check_movable_place(location, place);\n1735: \n1736:                 //          (Deep, Write(WriteKind::Move)),\n1741:                     LocalMutationIsAllowed::Yes,\n1742:                     state,\n1743:                 );\n1744: \n1745:                 // Finally, check if path was already moved.\n1746:                 self.check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved(\n1747:                     location,\n1748:                     InitializationRequiringAction::Use,\n1749:                     (place.as_ref(), span),\n1750:                     state,\n1751:                 );\n1752:             }\n1753:             Operand::Constant(_) => {}\n1754:         }\n1755:     }\n1756: \n1757:     /// Checks whether a borrow of this place is invalidated when the function\n1758:     /// exits\n1759:     #[instrument(level = \"debug\", skip(self))]\n1760:     fn check_for_invalidation_at_exit(\n1761:         &mut self,\n1762:         location: Location,\n1763:         borrow: &BorrowData<'tcx>,\n1764:         span: Span,\n1765:     ) {\n1766:         let place = borrow.borrowed_place;\n1767:         let mut root_place = PlaceRef { local: place.local, projection: &[] };\n1768: \n1769:         // For now\n1770:         // we just know that all locals are dropped at function exit (otherwise\n1771:         // we'll have a memory leak) and assume that all statics have a destructor.\n1772:         //\n1773:         // FIXME: allow thread-locals to borrow other thread locals?\n1774:         let might_be_alive = if self.body.local_decls[root_place.local].is_ref_to_thread_local() {\n1775:             // Thread-locals might be dropped after the function exits\n1776:             // We have to dereference the outer reference because\n1777:             // borrows don't conflict behind shared references.\n1778:             root_place.projection = TyCtxtConsts::DEREF_PROJECTION;\n1779:             true\n1780:         } else {\n1781:             false\n1782:         };\n1783: \n1784:         let sd = if might_be_alive { Deep } else { Shallow(None) };\n1785: \n1786:         if places_conflict::borrow_conflicts_with_place(\n1787:             self.infcx.tcx,\n1788:             self.body,\n1789:             place,\n1790:             borrow.kind,\n1791:             root_place,\n1792:             sd,\n1793:             places_conflict::PlaceConflictBias::Overlap,\n1794:         ) {\n1795:             debug!(\"check_for_invalidation_at_exit({:?}): INVALID\", place);\n1796:             // FIXME: should be talking about the region lifetime instead\n1797:             // of just a span here.\n1798:             let span = self.infcx.tcx.sess.source_map().end_point(span);\n1799:             self.report_borrowed_value_does_not_live_long_enough(\n1800:                 location,\n1801:                 borrow,\n1802:                 (place, span),\n1803:                 None,\n1804:             )\n1805:         }\n1806:     }\n1807: \n1808:     /// Reports an error if this is a borrow of local data.\n1809:     /// This is called for all Yield expressions on movable coroutines\n1810:     fn check_for_local_borrow(&mut self, borrow: &BorrowData<'tcx>, yield_span: Span) {\n1811:         debug!(\"check_for_local_borrow({:?})\", borrow);\n1812: \n1813:         if borrow_of_local_data(borrow.borrowed_place) {\n1814:             let err = self.cannot_borrow_across_coroutine_yield(\n1815:                 self.retrieve_borrow_spans(borrow).var_or_use(),\n1816:                 yield_span,\n1817:             );\n1818: \n1819:             self.buffer_error(err);\n1820:         }\n1821:     }\n1822: \n1823:     fn check_activations(&mut self, location: Location, span: Span, state: &BorrowckDomain) {\n1824:         // Two-phase borrow support: For each activation that is newly\n1825:         // generated at this statement, check if it interferes with\n1826:         // another borrow.\n1827:         for &borrow_index in self.borrow_set.activations_at_location(location) {\n1828:             let borrow = &self.borrow_set[borrow_index];\n1829: \n1830:             // only mutable borrows should be 2-phase\n1831:             assert!(match borrow.kind {\n1832:                 BorrowKind::Shared | BorrowKind::Fake(_) => false,\n1833:                 BorrowKind::Mut { .. } => true,\n1834:             });\n1835: \n1836:             self.access_place(\n1837:                 location,\n1838:                 (borrow.borrowed_place, span),\n1839:                 (Deep, Activation(WriteKind::MutableBorrow(borrow.kind), borrow_index)),\n1840:                 LocalMutationIsAllowed::No,\n1841:                 state,\n1842:             );\n1843:             // We do not need to call `check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved`\n1844:             // again, as we already called it when we made the\n1845:             // initial reservation.\n1846:         }\n1847:     }\n1848: \n1849:     fn check_movable_place(&mut self, location: Location, place: Place<'tcx>) {\n1850:         use IllegalMoveOriginKind::*;\n1851: \n1852:         let body = self.body;\n1853:         let tcx = self.infcx.tcx;\n1854:         let mut place_ty = PlaceTy::from_ty(body.local_decls[place.local].ty);\n1855:         for (place_ref, elem) in place.iter_projections() {\n1856:             match elem                 target_place: place_ref.project_deeper(&[elem], tcx),\n1864:                             },\n1865:                         ));\n1866:                         return;\n1867:                     }\n1868:                     ty::Adt(adt, _) => {\n1869:                         if !adt.is_box() {\n1870:                             bug!(\"Adt should be a box type when Place is deref\");\n1871:                         }\n1872:                     }\n1873:                     ty::Bool\n1874:                     | ty::Char\n1875:                     | ty::Int(_)\n1876:                     | ty::Uint(_)\n1877:                     | ty::Float(_)\n1878:                     | ty::Foreign(_)\n1879:                     | ty::Str\n1880:                     | ty::Array(_, _)\n1881:                     | ty::Pat(_, _)\n1882:                     | ty::Slice(_)\n1883:                     | ty::FnDef(_, _)\n1884:                     | ty::FnPtr(..)\n1885:                     | ty::Dynamic(_, _)\n1886:                     | ty::Closure(_, _)\n1887:                     | ty::CoroutineClosure(_, _)\n1888:                     | ty::Coroutine(_, _)\n1889:                     | ty::CoroutineWitness(..)\n1890:                     | ty::Never\n1891:                     | ty::Tuple(_)\n1892:                     | ty::UnsafeBinder(_)\n1893:                     | ty::Alias(_, _)\n1894:                     | ty::Param(_)\n1895:                     | ty::Bound(_, _)\n1896:                     | ty::Infer(_)\n1897:                     | ty::Error(_)\n1898:                     | ty::Placeholder(_) => {\n1899:                         bug!(\"When Place is Deref it's type shouldn't be {place_ty:#?}\")\n1900:                     }\n1901:                 },\n1902:                 ProjectionElem::Field(_, _) => match place_ty.ty.kind() {\n1903:                     ty::Adt(adt, _) => {\n1904:                         if adt.has_dtor(tcx) {\n1905:                             self.move_errors.push(MoveError::new(\n1906:                                 place,\n1907:                                 location,\n1908:                                 InteriorOfTypeWithDestructor { container_ty: place_ty.ty },\n1909:                             ));\n1910:                             return;\n1911:                         }\n1912:                     }\n1913: ty::Bool\n1918:                     | ty::Char\n1919:                     | ty::Int(_)\n1920:                     | ty::Uint(_)\n1921:                     | ty::Float(_)\n1922:                     | ty::Foreign(_)\n1923:                     | ty::Str\n1924:                     | ty::Array(_, _)\n1925:                     | ty::Pat(_, _)\n1926:                     | ty::Slice(_)\n1927:                     | ty::RawPtr(_, _)\n1928:                     | ty::Ref(_, _, _)\n1929:                     | ty::FnDef(_, _)\n1930:                     | ty::FnPtr(..)\n1931:                     | ty::Dynamic(_, _)\n1932:                     | ty::CoroutineWitness(..)\n1933:                     | ty::Never\n1934:                     | ty::UnsafeBinder(_)\n1935:                     | ty::Alias(_, _)\n1936:                     | ty::Param(_)\n1937:                     | ty::Bound(_, _)\n1938:                     | ty::Infer(_)\n1939:                     | ty::Error(_)\n1940:                     | ty::Placeholder(_) => bug!(\n1941:                         \"When Place contains ProjectionElem::Field it's type shouldn't be {place_ty:#?}\"\n1942:                     ),\n1943:                 },\n1944:                 ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { .. } | ProjectionElem::Subslice { .. } => {\n1945:                     match place_ty.ty.kind() {\n1946:                         ty::Slice(_) => {\n1947:                             self.move_errors.push(MoveError::new(\n1948:                                 place,\n1949:                                 location,\n1950:                                 InteriorOfSliceOrArray { ty: place_ty.ty, is_index: false },\n1951:                             ));\n1952:                             return;\n1953:                         }\n1954:                         ty::Array(_, _) => (),\n1955:                         _ => bug!(\"Unexpected type {:#?}\", place_ty.ty),\n1956:                     }\n1957:                 }\n1958:                 ProjectionElem::Index(_) => match place_ty.ty.kind() {\n1959:                     ty::Array(..) | ty::Slice(..) => {\n1960:                         self.move_errors.push(MoveError::new(\n1961:                             place,\n1962:                             location,\n1963:                             InteriorOfSliceOrArray { ty: place_ty.ty, is_index: true },\n1964:                         ));\n1965:                         return;\n1966:                     }\n1967:                     _ => bug!(\"Unexpected type {place_ty:#?}\"),\n1968:                 },\n1969:                 // `OpaqueCast`: only transmutes the type, so no moves there.\n1970:                 // `Downcast`  : only changes information about a `Place` without moving.\n1971:                 // So it's safe to skip these.\n1972:                 ProjectionElem::OpaqueCast(_)\n1973:                 | ProjectionElem::Downcast(_, _)\n1974:                 | ProjectionElem::UnwrapUnsafeBinder(_) => (),\n1975:             }\n1976: \n1977:             place_ty = place_ty.projection_ty(tcx, elem);\n1978:         }\n1979:     }\n1980: \n1981:     fn check_if_full_path_is_moved(\n1982:         &mut self,\n1983:         location: Location,\n1984:         desired_action: InitializationRequiringAction,\n1985:         place_span: (PlaceRef<'tcx>, Span),\n1986:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n1987:     ) {\n1988:         let maybe_uninits = &state.uninits;\n1989: \n1990:         // Bad scenarios:\n1991:         //\n1992:         // 1. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a.b.c`\n1993:         // 2. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a.b.c.d` (without first reinitializing `a.b.c.d`)\n1994:         // 3. Uninitialized `(a.b.c: &_)`, use of `*a.b.c`; note that with\n1995:         //    partial initialization support, one might have `a.x`\n1996:         //    initialized but not `a.b`.\n1997:         //\n1998:         // OK scenarios:\n1999:         //\n2000:         // 4. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a.b.d`\n2001:         // 5. Uninitialized `a.x`, initialized `a.b`, use of `a.b`\n2002:         // 6. Copied `(a.b: &_)`, use of `*(a.b).c`; note that `a.b`\n2003:         //    must have been initialized for the use to be sound.\n2004:         // 7. Move of `a.b.c` then reinit of `a.b.c.d`, use of `a.b.c.d`\n2005: \n2006:         // The dataflow tracks shallow prefixes distinctly (that is,\n2007:         // field-accesses on P distinctly from P itself), in order to\n2008:         // track substructure initialization separately from the whole\n2009:         // structure.\n2010:         //\n2011:         // E.g., when looking at (*a.b.c).d, if the closest prefix for\n2012:         // which we have a MovePath is `a.b`, then that means that the\n2013:         // initialization state of `a.b` is all we need to inspect to\n2014:         // know if `a.b.c` is valid (and from that we infer that the\n2015:         // dereference and `.d` access is also valid, since we assume\n2016:         // `a.b.c` is assigned a reference to an initialized and\n2017:         // well-formed record structure.)\n2018: \n2019:         // Therefore, if we seek out the *closest* prefix for which we\n2020:         // have a MovePath, that should capture the initialization\n2021:         // state for the place scenario.\n2022:         //\n2023:         // This code covers scenarios 1, 2, and 3.\n2024: \n2025:         debug!(\"check_if_full_path_is_moved place: {:?}\", place_span.0);\n2026:         let (prefix, mpi) = self.move_path_closest_to(place_span.0);\n2027:         if maybe_uninits.contains(mpi) {\n2028:             self.report_use_of_moved_or_uninitialized(\n2029:                 location,\n2030:                 desired_action,\n2031:                 (prefix, place_span.0, place_span.1),\n2032:                 mpi,\n2033:             );\n2034:         } // Only query longest prefix with a MovePath, not further\n2035:         // ancestors; dataflow recurs on children when parents\n2036:         // move (to support partial (re)inits).\n2037:         //\n2038:         // (I.e., querying parents breaks scenario 7; but may want\n2039:         // to do such a query based on partial-init feature-gate.)\n2040:     }\n2041: \n2042:     /// Subslices correspond to multiple move paths, so we iterate through the\n2043:     /// elements of the base array. For each element we check\n2044:     ///\n2045:     /// * Does this element overlap with our slice.\n2046:     /// * Is any part of it uninitialized.\n2047:     fn check_if_subslice_element_is_moved(\n2048:         &mut self,\n2049:         location: Location,\n2050:         desired_action: InitializationRequiringAction,\n2051:         place_span: (PlaceRef<'tcx>, Span),\n2052:         maybe_uninits: &MixedBitSet<MovePathIndex>,\n2053:         from: u64,\n2054:         to: u64,\n2055:     ) {\n2056:         if let Some(mpi) = self.move_path_for_place(place_span.0) {\n2057:             let move_paths = &self.move_data.move_paths;\n2058: \n2059:             let root_path = &move_paths[mpi];\n2060:             for (child_mpi, child_move_path) in root_path.children(move_paths) {\n2061:                 let last_proj = child_move_path.place.projection.last().unwrap();\n2062:                 if let ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { offset, from_end, .. } = last_proj {\n2063:                     debug_assert!(!from_end, \"Array constant indexing shouldn't be `from_end`.\");\n2064: \n2065:                     if (from..to).contains(offset) {\n2066:                         let uninit_child =\n2067:                             self.move_data.find_in_move_path_or_its_descendants(child_mpi, |mpi| {\n2068:                                 maybe_uninits.contains(mpi)\n2069:                             });\n2070: \n2071:                         if let Some(uninit_child) = uninit_child {\n2072:                             self.report_use_of_moved_or_uninitialized(\n2073:                                 location,\n2074:                                 desired_action,\n2075:                                 (place_span.0, place_span.0, place_span.1),\n2076:                                 uninit_child,\n2077:                             );\n2078:                             return; // don't bother finding other problems.\n2079:                         }\n2080:                     }\n2081:                 }\n2082:             }\n2083:         }\n2084:     }\n2085: \n2086:     fn check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved(\n2087:         &mut self,\n2088:         location: Location,\n2089:         desired_action: InitializationRequiringAction,\n2090:         place_span: (PlaceRef<'tcx>, Span),\n2091:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n2092:     ) {\n2093:         let maybe_uninits = &state.uninits;\n2094: \n2095:         // Bad scenarios:\n2096:         //\n2097:         // 1. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a` or `a.b`\n2098:         //    partial initialization support, one might have `a.x`\n2099:         //    initialized but not `a.b`.\n2100:         // 2. All bad scenarios from `check_if_full_path_is_moved`\n2101:         //\n2102:         // OK scenarios:\n2103:         //\n2104:         // 3. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a.b.d`\n2105:         // 4. Uninitialized `a.x`, initialized `a.b`, use of `a.b`\n2106:         // 5. Copied `(a.b: &_)`, use of `*(a.b).c`; note that `a.b`\n2107:         //    must have been initialized for the use to be sound.\n2108:         // 6. This is scenario 3 above.\n2131:         //\n2132:         // (Distinct from handling of scenarios 1+2+4 above because\n2133:         // `place` does not interfere with suffixes of its prefixes,\n2134:         // e.g., `a.b.c` does not interfere with `a.b.d`)\n2135:         //\n2136:         // This code covers scenario 1.\n2137: \n2138:         debug!(\"check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved place: {:?}\", place_span.0);\n2139:         if let Some(mpi) = self.move_path_for_place(place_span.0) {\n2140:             let uninit_mpi = self\n2141:                 .move_data\n2142:                 .find_in_move_path_or_its_descendants(mpi, |mpi| maybe_uninits.contains(mpi));\n2143: \n2144:             if let Some(uninit_mpi) = uninit_mpi {\n2145:                 self.report_use_of_moved_or_uninitialized(\n2146:                     location,\n2147:                     desired_action,\n2148:                     (place_span.0, place_span.0, place_span.1),\n2149:                     uninit_mpi,\n2150:                 );\n2151:                 return; // don't bother finding other problems.\n2152:             }\n2153:         }\n2154:     }\n2155: \n2156:     /// Currently MoveData does not store entries for all places in\n2157:     /// the input MIR. For example it will currently filter out\n2158:     /// places that are Copy; thus we do not track places of shared\n2159:     /// reference type. This routine will walk up a place along its\n2160:     /// prefixes, searching for a foundational place that *is*\n2161:     /// tracked in the MoveData.\n2162:     ///\n2163:     /// An Err result includes a tag indicated why the search failed.\n2164:     /// Currently this can only occur if the place is built off of a\n2165:     /// static variable, as we do not track those in the MoveData.\n2166:     fn move_path_closest_to(&mut self, place: PlaceRef<'tcx>) -> (PlaceRef<'tcx>, MovePathIndex) {\n2167:         match self.move_data.rev_lookup.find(place) {\n2168:             LookupResult::Parent(Some(mpi)) | LookupResult::Exact(mpi) => {\n2169:                 (self.move_data.move_paths[mpi].place.as_ref(), mpi)\n2170:             }\n2171:             LookupResult::Parent(None) => panic!(\"should have move path for every Local\"),\n2172:         }\n2173:     }\n2174: \n2175:     fn move_path_for_place(&mut self, place: PlaceRef<'tcx>) -> Option<MovePathIndex> {\n2176:         // If returns None, then there is no move path corresponding\n2177:         // to a direct owner of `place` (which means there is nothing\n2178:         // that => Some(mpi),\n2183:         }\n2184:     }\n2185: \n2186:     fn check_if_assigned_path_is_moved(\n2187:         &mut self,\n2188:         location: Location,\n2189:         (place, span): (Place<'tcx>, Span),\n2190:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n2191:     ) {\n2192:         debug!(\"check_if_assigned_path_is_moved place: {:?}\", place);\n2193: \n2194:         // None case => assigning to `x` does not require `x` be initialized.\n2195:         for (place_base, elem) in place.iter_projections().rev() {\n2196:             match elem {\n2197: ProjectionElem::UnwrapUnsafeBinder(_) => {\n2208:                     check_parent_of_field(self, location, place_base, span, state);\n2209:                 }\n2210: \n2211:                 // further)\n2218:                     break;\n2219:                 }\n2220: \n2221:                 ProjectionElem::Subslice { .. } => {\n2222:                     panic!(\"we don't allow assignments to subslices, location: {location:?}\");\n2223:                 }\n2224: \n2225:                 ProjectionElem::Field(..) => {\n2226:                     // if type of `P` has a dtor, then\n2227:                     // assigning to `P.f` requires `P` itself\n2228:                     // be already initialized\n2229:                     let tcx = self.infcx.tcx;\n2230:                     let    self.check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved(\n2234:                                 location, InitializationRequiringAction::Assignment,\n2235:                                 (place_base, span),          }\n2241: \n2242:                         // Once `let s; s.x = V; read(s.x);`,\n2243:                         // is allowed, remove this match arm.\n2244:                         ty::Adt(..) | ty::Tuple(..) => {\n2245:                             check_parent_of_field(self, location, place_base, span, state);\n2246:                         }\n2247: \n2248:                         _ => {}\n2249:                     }\n2250:                 }\n2251:             }\n2252:         }\n2253: \n2254:         fn check_parent_of_field<'a, 'tcx>(\n2255:             this: &mut MirBorrowckCtxt<'a, '_, 'tcx>,\n2256:             location: Location,\n2257:             base: PlaceRef<'tcx>,\n2258:             span: Span,\n2259:             state: &BorrowckDomain,\n2260:         ) {\n2261:             // rust-lang/rust#21232: Until Rust allows reads from the\n2262:             // initialized parts of partially initialized structs, we\n2263:             // will, starting with the 2018 edition, reject attempts\n2264:             // to write to structs that are not fully initialized.\n2265:             //\n2266:             // In other words, *until* we allow this:\n2267:             //\n2268:             // 1. `let mut s; s.x = Val; read(s.x);`\n2269:             //\n2270:             // we will for now disallow this:\n2271:             //\n2272:             // 2. `let mut s; s.x = Val;`\n2273:             //\n2274:             // and also this:\n2275:             //\n2276:             // 3. `let mut s = ...; drop(s); s.x=Val;`\n2277:             //\n2278:             // This does not use check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved,\n2279:             // because we want to *allow* reinitializations of fields:\n2280:             // e.g., want to allow\n2281:             //\n2282:             // `let mut s = ...; drop(s.x); s.x=Val;`\n2283:             //\n2284:             // This does not use check_if_full_path_is_moved on\n2285:             // `base`, because that would report an error about the\n2286:             // `base` as a whole, but in this scenario we *really*\n2287:             // want to report an error about the actual thing that was\n2288:             // moved, which may be some prefix of `base`.\n2289: \n2290:             // Shallow so that we'll stop at any dereference; we'll\n2291:             // report errors about issues with such bases elsewhere.\n2292:             let maybe_uninits = &state.uninits;\n2293: \n2294:             // Find the shortest uninitialized prefix you can reach\n2295:             // without going over a Deref.\n2296:             let mut shortest_uninit_seen = None;\n2297:             for prefix in this.prefixes(base, PrefixSet::Shallow) {\n2298:                 let Some(mpi) = this.move_path_for_place(prefix) else { continue };\n2299: \n2300:                 if maybe_uninits.contains(mpi) {\n2301:                     debug!(\n2302:                         \"check_parent_of_field updating shortest_uninit_seen from {:?} to {:?}\",\n2303:                         shortest_uninit_seen,\n2304:                         Some((prefix, mpi))\n2305:                     );\n2306:                     shortest_uninit_seen = Some((prefix, mpi));\n2307:                 } else {\n2308:                     debug!(\"check_parent_of_field {:?} is definitely initialized\", (prefix, mpi));\n2309:                 }\n2310:             }\n2311: \n2312:             if let Some((prefix, mpi)) = shortest_uninit_seen {\n2313:                 // Check for a reassignment into an uninitialized field of a union (for example,\n2314:                 // after a move out). In this case, do not report an error here. There is an\n2315:                 // exception, if this is the first assignment into the union (that is, there is\n2316:                 // no move out from an earlier location) then this is an attempt at initialization\n2317:                 // of the union - we should error in that case.\n2318:                 let tcx = this.infcx.tcx;\n2319:                 if base.ty(this.body(), tcx).ty.is_union()\n2320:                     && this.move_data.path_map[mpi].iter().any(|moi| {\n2321:                         this.move_data.moves[*moi].source.is_predecessor_of(location, this.body)\n2322:                     })\n2323:                 {\n2324:                     return;\n2325:                 }\n2326: \n2327:                 this.report_use_of_moved_or_uninitialized(\n2328:                     location,\n2329:                     InitializationRequiringAction::PartialAssignment,\n2330:                     (prefix, base, span),\n2331:                     mpi,\n2332:                 );\n2333: \n2334:                 // rust-lang/rust#21232, #54499, #54986: during period where we reject\n2335:                 // partial initialization, do not complain about unnecessary `mut` on\n2336:                 // an attempt to do a partial initialization.\n2337:                 this.used_mut.insert(base.local);\n2338:             }\n2339:         }\n2340:     }\n2341: \n2342:     /// Checks the permissions for the given place and read or write kind\n2343:     ///\n2344:     /// Returns `true` if an error is reported.\n2345:     fn check_access_permissions(\n2346:         &mut self,\n2347:         (place, span): (Place<'tcx>, Span),\n2348:         kind: ReadOrWrite,\n2349:         is_local_mutation_allowed: LocalMutationIsAllowed,\n2350:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n2351:         location: Location,\n2352:     ) -> bool {\n2353:         debug!(\n2354:             \"check_access_permissions({:?}, {:?}, is_local_mutation_allowed: {:?})\",\n2355:             place, kind, is_local_mutation_allowed\n2356:         );\n2357: \n2358:         let error_access;\n2359:         let the_place_err;\n2360: \n2361:         match kind {\n2362:             Reservation(WriteKind::MutableBorrow(BorrowKind::Mut { kind: mut_borrow_kind }))\n2363:             | Write(WriteKind::MutableBorrow(BorrowKind::Mut { kind: mut_borrow_kind })) => {\n2364:                 let is_local_mutation_allowed = match mut_borrow_kind {\n2365:                     // `ClosureCapture` is used for mutable variable with an immutable binding.\n2366:                     // This is only behaviour difference between `ClosureCapture` and mutable\n2367:                     // borrows.\n2368:                     MutBorrowKind::ClosureCapture => LocalMutationIsAllowed::Yes,\n2369:                     MutBorrowKind::Default | MutBorrowKind::TwoPhaseBorrow => {\n2370:                         is_local_mutation_allowed\n2371:                     }\n2372:                 };\n2373:                 match self.is_mutable(place.as_ref(), is_local_mutation_allowed) {\n2374:                     Ok(root_place) => {\n2375:                         self.add_used_mut(root_place, state);\n2376:                         return false;\n2377:                     }\n2378:                     Err(place_err) => {\n2379:                         error_access = AccessKind::MutableBorrow;\n2380:                         the_place_err = place_err;\n2381:                     }\n2382:                 }\n2383:             }\n2384:             Reservation(WriteKind::Mutate) | Write(WriteKind::Mutate) => {\n2385:                 match self.is_mutable(place.as_ref(), is_local_mutation_allowed) {\n2386:                     Ok(root_place) => {\n2387:                         self.add_used_mut(root_place, state);\n2388:                         return false;\n2389:                     }\n2390:                     Err(place_err) => {\n2391:                         error_access = AccessKind::Mutate;\n2392:                         the_place_err = place_err;\n2393:                     }\n2394:                 }\n2395:             }\n2396: \n2397:             Reservation(\n2398:                 WriteKind::Move\n2399:                 | WriteKind::Replace\n2400:                 | WriteKind::StorageDeadOrDrop\n2401:                 | WriteKind::MutableBorrow(BorrowKind::Shared)\n2402:                 | WriteKind::MutableBorrow(BorrowKind::Fake(_)),\n2403:             )\n2404:             | Write(\n2405:                 WriteKind::Move\n2406:                 | WriteKind::Replace\n2407:                 | WriteKind::StorageDeadOrDrop\n2408:                 | WriteKind::MutableBorrow(BorrowKind::Shared)\n2409:                 | WriteKind::MutableBorrow(BorrowKind::Fake(_)),\n2410:             ) => {\n2411:                 if self.is_mutable(place.as_ref(), is_local_mutation_allowed).is_err()\n2412:                     && !self.has_buffered_diags()\n2413:                 {\n2414:                     // rust-lang/rust#46908: In pure NLL mode this code `-Ztreat-err-as-bug`\n2417:                     // enabled. We don't want to ICE for that case, as other errors will have\n2418:                     // been emitted (#52262).\n2419:                     self.dcx().span_delayed_bug(\n2420:                         span,\n2421:                         format!(\n2422:                             \"Accessing `{place:?}` with the kind `{kind:?}` shouldn't be possible\",\n2423:                         ),\n2424:                     );\n2425:                 }\n2426:                 return false;\n2427:             }\n2428:             Activation(..) => {\n2429:                 // permission checks are done at Reservation point.\n2430:                 return false;\n2431:             }\n2432:             Read(\n2433:                 ReadKind::Borrow(BorrowKind::Mut { .. } | BorrowKind::Shared | BorrowKind::Fake(_))\n2434:                 | ReadKind::Copy,\n2435:             ) => {\n2436:                 // Access authorized\n2437:                 return false;\n2438:             }\n2439:         }\n2440: \n2441:         // rust-lang/rust#21232, #54986: during period where we reject\n2442:         // partial initialization, do not complain about mutability\n2443:         // errors except self.report_illegal_reassignment((place, span), assigned_span, place);\n2455:             } else {\n2456:                 self.report_mutability_error(place, span, the_place_err, error_access, location)\n2457:             }\n2458:             true\n2459:         } else {\n2460:             false\n2461:         }\n2462:     }\n2463: \n2464:     fn is_local_ever_initialized(&self, local: Local, state: &BorrowckDomain) -> Option<InitIndex> {\n2465:         let mpi = self.move_data.rev_lookup.find_local(local)?;\n2466:         let ii = &self.move_data.init_path_map[mpi];\n2467:         ii.into_iter().find(|&&index| state.ever_inits.contains(index)).copied()\n2468:     }\n2469: \n2470:     /// Adds the place into the used mutable variables set\n2471:     fn add_used_mut(&mut self,  /// Whether this value can be written or borrowed mutably.\n2504:     /// Returns the root place if the place passed in is a projection.\n2505:     fn is_mutable(\n2506:         &self,\n2507: up and say that they might conflict. This occurs when\n2700:     /// different fields of a union are borrowed. For example,\n2701:     /// if `u` is a union, we have no way of telling how disjoint\n2702:     /// `u.a.x` and `a.b.y` are.\n2703:     Arbitrary,\n2704:     /// The places have the same type, and are either completely disjoint\n2705:     /// or equal - i.e., they can't \"partially\" overlap as can occur with\n2706:     /// unions. This is the \"base case\" on which we recur for extensions\n2707:     /// of the place.\n2708:     EqualOrDisjoint,\n2709:     /// The places are disjoint, so we know all extensions of them\n2710:     /// will also be disjoint.\n2711:     Disjoint,\n2712: }\n2713: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/lib.rs"}}}
{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01LRErcPS8Zi1TCKuj6HD4cY","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: //! The borrowck rules for proving disjointness are applied from the \\\"root\\\" of the\\n2: //! borrow forwards, iterating over \\\"similar\\\" projections in lockstep until\\n3: //! we can prove overlap one way or another. Essentially, we treat `Overlap` as\\n4: //! a monoid and report a conflict if the product ends up not being `Disjoint`.\\n5: //!\\n6: //! On each step, if we didn't run out of borrow or place, we know that our elements\\n7: //! have the same type, and that they only overlap if they are the identical.\\n8: //!\\n9: //! For example, if we are comparing these:\\n10: //! ```text\\n11: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\\n12: //! ACCESS:  (*x1[i].y).w.b\\n13: //! ```\\n14: //!\\n15: //! Then our steps are:\\n16: //! ```text\\n17: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\\n18: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\\n19: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n20: //!      *x1[2].y    |  *x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n21: //!     (*x1[2].y).z | (*x1[i].y).w  -- we are disjoint and don't need to check more!\\n22: //! ```\\n23: //!\\n24: //! Because `zip` does potentially bad things to the iterator inside, this loop\\n25: //! also handles the case where the access might be a *prefix* of the borrow, e.g.\\n26: //!\\n27: //! ```text\\n28: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\\n29: //! ACCESS:  x1[i].y\\n30: //! ```\\n31: //!\\n32: //! Then our steps are:\\n33: //! ```text\\n34: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\\n35: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\\n36: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n37: //! ```\\n38: //!\\n39: //! -- here we run out of access - the borrow can access a part of it. If this\\n40: //! is a full deep access, then we *know* the borrow conflicts with it. However,\\n41: //! if the access is shallow, then we can proceed:\\n42: //!\\n43: //! ```text\\n44: //!       x1[2].y    | (*x1[i].y)    -- a deref! the access can't get past this, so we\\n45: //!                                     are disjoint\\n46: //! ```\\n47: //!\\n48: //! Our invariant is, that at each step of the iteration:\\n49: //!  - If we didn't run out of access to match, our borrow and access are comparable\\n50: //!    and either equal or disjoint.\\n51: //!  - If we did run out of access, the borrow can access a part of it.\\n52: \\n53: use std::cmp::max;\\n54: use std::iter;\\n55: \\n56: use rustc_hir as hir;\\n57: use rustc_middle::bug;\\n58: use rustc_middle::mir::{\\n59:     Body, BorrowKind, FakeBorrowKind, MutBorrowKind, Place, PlaceElem, PlaceRef, ProjectionElem,\\n60: };\\n61: use rustc_middle::ty::{self, TyCtxt};\\n62: use tracing::{debug, instrument};\\n63: \\n64: use crate::{AccessDepth, ArtificialField, Deep, Overlap, Shallow};\\n65: \\n66: /// When checking if a place conflicts with another place, this enum is used to influence decisions\\n67: /// where a place might be equal or disjoint with another place, such as if `a[i] == a[j]`.\\n68: /// `PlaceConflictBias::Overlap` would bias toward assuming that `i` might equal `j` and that these\\n69: /// places overlap. `PlaceConflictBias::NoOverlap` assumes that for the purposes of the predicate\\n70: /// being run in the calling context, the conservative choice is to assume the compared indices\\n71: /// are disjoint (and therefore, do not overlap).\\n72: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug, Eq, PartialEq)]\\n73: pub enum PlaceConflictBias {\\n74:     Overlap,\\n75:     NoOverlap,\\n76: }\\n77: \\n78: /// Helper function for checking if places conflict with a mutable borrow and deep access depth.\\n79: /// This is used to check for places conflicting outside of the borrow checking code (such as in\\n80: /// dataflow).\\n81: pub fn places_conflict<'tcx>(\\n82:     tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\\n83:     body: &Body<'tcx>,\\n84:     borrow_place: Place<'tcx>,\\n85:     access_place: Place<'tcx>,\\n86:     bias: PlaceConflictBias,\\n87: ) -> bool {\\n88:     borrow_conflicts_with_place(\\n89:         tcx,\\n90:         body,\\n91:         borrow_place,\\n92:         BorrowKind::Mut { kind: MutBorrowKind::TwoPhaseBorrow },\\n93:         access_place.as_ref(),\\n94:         AccessDepth::Deep,\\n95:         bias,\\n96:     )\\n97: }\\n98: \\n99: /// Checks whether the `borrow_place` conflicts with the `access_place` given a borrow kind and\\n100: /// access depth. The `bias` parameter is used to determine how the unknowable (comparing runtime\\n101: /// array indices, for example) should be interpreted - this depends on what the caller wants in\\n102: /// order to make the conservative choice and preserve soundness.\\n103: #[inline]\\n104: pub(super) fn borrow_conflicts_with_place<'tcx>(\\n105:     tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\\n106:     body: &Body<'tcx>,\\n107:     borrow_place: Place<'tcx>,\\n108:     borrow_kind: BorrowKind,\\n109:     access_place: PlaceRef<'tcx>,\\n110:     access: AccessDepth,\\n111:     bias: PlaceConflictBias,\\n112: ) -> bool {\\n113:     let borrow_local = borrow_place.local;\\n114:     let access_local = access_place.local;\\n115: \\n116:     if borrow_local != access_local {\\n117:         // We have proven the borrow disjoint - further projections will remain disjoint.\\n118:         return false;\\n119:     }\\n120: \\n121:     // This Local/Local case is handled by the more general code below, but\\n122:     // it's so common that it's a speed win to check for it first.\\n123:     if borrow_place.projection.is_empty() && access_place.projection.is_empty() {\\n124:         return true;\\n125:     }\\n126: \\n127:     place_components_conflict(tcx, body, borrow_place, borrow_kind, access_place, access, bias)\\n128: }\\n129: \\n130: #[instrument(level = \\\"debug\\\", skip(tcx, body))]\\n131: fn place_components_conflict<'tcx>(\\n132:     tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\\n133:     body: &Body<'tcx>,\\n134:     borrow_place: Place<'tcx>,\\n135:     borrow_kind: BorrowKind,\\n136:     access_place: PlaceRef<'tcx>,\\n137:     access: AccessDepth,\\n138:     bias: PlaceConflictBias,\\n139: ) -> bool {\\n140:     let borrow_local = borrow_place.local;\\n141:     let access_local = access_place.local;\\n142:     // borrow_conflicts_with_place should have checked that.\\n143:     assert_eq!(borrow_local, access_local);\\n144: \\n145:     // loop invariant: borrow_c is always either equal to access_c or disjoint from it.\\n146:     for ((borrow_place, borrow_c), &access_c) in\\n147:         iter::zip(borrow_place.iter_projections(), access_place.projection)\\n148:     {\\n149:         debug!(?borrow_c, ?access_c);\\n150: \\n151:         // Borrow and access path both have more components.\\n152:         //\\n153:         // Examples:\\n154:         //\\n155:         // - borrow of `a.(...)`, access to `a.(...)`\\n156:         // - borrow of `a.(...)`, access to `b.(...)`\\n157:         //\\n158:         // Here we only see the components we have checked so\\n159:         // far (in our examples, just the first component). We\\n160:         // check whether the components being borrowed vs\\n161:         // accessed are disjoint (as in the second example,\\n162:         // but not the first).\\n163:         match place_projection_conflict(tcx, body, borrow_place, borrow_c, access_c, bias) {\\n164:             Overlap::Arbitrary => {\\n165:                 // We have encountered different fields of potentially\\n166:                 // the same union - the borrow now partially overlaps.\\n167:                 //\\n168:                 // There is no *easy* way of comparing the fields\\n169:                 // further on, because they might have different types\\n170:                 // (e.g., borrows of `u.a.0` and `u.b.y` where `.0` and\\n171:                 // `.y` come from different structs).\\n172:                 //\\n173:                 // We could try to do some things here - e.g., count\\n174:                 // dereferences - but that's probably not a good\\n175:                 // idea, at least for now, so just give up and\\n176:                 // report a conflict. This is unsafe code anyway so\\n177:                 // the user could always use raw pointers.\\n178:                 debug!(\\\"arbitrary -> conflict\\\");\\n179:                 return true;\\n180:             }\\n181:             Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint => {\\n182:                 // This is the recursive case - proceed to the next element.\\n183:             }\\n184:             Overlap::Disjoint => {\\n185:                 // We have proven the borrow disjoint - further\\n186:                 // projections will remain disjoint.\\n187:                 debug!(\\\"disjoint\\\");\\n188:                 return false;\\n189:             }\\n190:         }\\n191:     }\\n192: \\n193:     if borrow_place.projection.len() > access_place.projection.len() {\\n194:         for (base, elem) in borrow_place.iter_projections().skip(access_place.projection.len()) {\\n195:             // Borrow path is longer than the access path. Examples:\\n196:             //\\n197:             // - borrow of `a.b.c`, access to `a.b`\\n198:             //\\n199:             // Here, we know that the borrow can access a part of\\n200:             // our place. This is a conflict if that is a part our\\n201:             // access cares about.\\n202: \\n203:             let base_ty = base.ty(body, tcx).ty;\\n204: \\n205:             match (elem, base_ty.kind(), access) {\\n206:                 (_, _, Shallow(Some(ArtificialField::ArrayLength)))\\n207:                 | (_, _, Shallow(Some(ArtificialField::FakeBorrow))) => {\\n208:                     // The array length is like additional fields on the\\n209:                     // type; it does not overlap any existing data there.\\n210:                     // Furthermore, if cannot actually be a prefix of any\\n211:                     // borrowed place (at least in MIR as it is currently.)\\n212:                     //\\n213:                     // e.g., a (mutable) borrow of `a[5]` while we read the\\n214:                     // array length of `a`.\\n215:                     debug!(\\\"borrow_conflicts_with_place: implicit field\\\");\\n216:                     return false;\\n217:                 }\\n218: \\n219:                 (ProjectionElem::Deref, _, Shallow(None)) => {\\n220:                     // e.g., a borrow of `*x.y` while we shallowly access `x.y` or some\\n221:                     // prefix thereof - the shallow access can't touch anything behind\\n222:                     // the pointer.\\n223:                     debug!(\\\"borrow_conflicts_with_place: shallow access behind ptr\\\");\\n224:                     return false;\\n225:                 }\\n226:                 (ProjectionElem::Deref, ty::Ref(_, _, hir::Mutability::Not), _) => {\\n227:                     // Shouldn't be tracked\\n228:                     bug!(\\\"Tracking borrow behind shared reference.\\\");\\n229:                 }\\n230:                 (ProjectionElem::Deref, ty::Ref(_, _, hir::Mutability::Mut), AccessDepth::Drop) => {\\n231:                     // Values behind a mutable reference are not access either by dropping a\\n232:                     // value, or by StorageDead\\n233:                     debug!(\\\"borrow_conflicts_with_place: drop access behind ptr\\\");\\n234:                     return false;\\n235:                 }\\n236: \\n237:                 (ProjectionElem::Field { .. }, ty::Adt(def, _), AccessDepth::Drop) => {\\n238:                     // Drop can read/write arbitrary projections, so places\\n239:                     // conflict regardless of further projections.\\n240:                     if def.has_dtor(tcx) {\\n241:                         return true;\\n242:                     }\\n243:                 }\\n244: \\n245:                 (ProjectionElem::Deref, _, Deep)\\n246:                 | (ProjectionElem::Deref, _, AccessDepth::Drop)\\n247:                 | (ProjectionElem::Field { .. }, _, _)\\n248:                 | (ProjectionElem::Index { .. }, _, _)\\n249:                 | (ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { .. }, _, _)\\n250:                 | (ProjectionElem::Subslice { .. }, _, _)\\n251:                 | (ProjectionElem::OpaqueCast { .. }, _, _)\\n252:                 | (ProjectionElem::Downcast { .. }, _, _)\\n253:                 | (ProjectionElem::UnwrapUnsafeBinder(_), _, _) => {\\n254:                     // Recursive case. This can still be disjoint on a\\n255:                     // further iteration if this a shallow access and\\n256:                     // there's a deref later on, e.g., a borrow\\n257:                     // of `*x.y` while accessing `x`.\\n258:                 }\\n259:             }\\n260:         }\\n261:     }\\n262: \\n263:     // Borrow path ran out but access path may not\\n264:     // have. Examples:\\n265:     //\\n266:     // - borrow of `a.b`, access to `a.b.c`\\n267:     // - borrow of `a.b`, access to `a.b`\\n268:     //\\n269:     // In the first example, where we didn't run out of\\n270:     // access, the borrow can access all of our place, so we\\n271:     // have a conflict.\\n272:     //\\n273:     // If the second example, where we did, then we still know\\n274:     // that the borrow can access a *part* of our place that\\n275:     // our access cares about, so we still have a conflict.\\n276:     if borrow_kind == BorrowKind::Fake(FakeBorrowKind::Shallow)\\n277:         && borrow_place.projection.len() < access_place.projection.len()\\n278:     {\\n279:         debug!(\\\"borrow_conflicts_with_place: shallow borrow\\\");\\n280:         false\\n281:     } else {\\n282:         debug!(\\\"borrow_conflicts_with_place: full borrow, CONFLICT\\\");\\n283:         true\\n284:     }\\n285: }\\n286: \\n287: // Given that the bases of `elem1` and `elem2` are always either equal\\n288: // or disjoint (and have the same type!), return the overlap situation\\n289: // between `elem1` and `elem2`.\\n290: fn place_projection_conflict<'tcx>(\\n291:     tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\\n292:     body: &Body<'tcx>,\\n293:     pi1: PlaceRef<'tcx>,\\n294:     pi1_elem: PlaceElem<'tcx>,\\n295:     pi2_elem: PlaceElem<'tcx>,\\n296:     bias: PlaceConflictBias,\\n297: ) -> Overlap {\\n298:     match (pi1_elem, pi2_elem) {\\n299:         (ProjectionElem::Deref, ProjectionElem::Deref) => {\\n300:             // derefs (e.g., `*x` vs. `*x`) - recur.\\n301:             debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-OR-EQ-DEREF\\\");\\n302:             Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint\\n303:         }\\n304:         (ProjectionElem::OpaqueCast(_), ProjectionElem::OpaqueCast(_)) => {\\n305:             // casts to other types may always conflict irrespective of the type being cast to.\\n306:             debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-OR-EQ-OPAQUE\\\");\\n307:             Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint\\n308:         }\\n309:         (ProjectionElem::Field(f1, _), ProjectionElem::Field(f2, _)) => {\\n310:             if f1 == f2 {\\n311:                 // same field (e.g., `a.y` vs. `a.y`) - recur.\\n312:                 debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-OR-EQ-FIELD\\\");\\n313:                 Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint\\n314:             } else {\\n315:                 let ty = pi1.ty(body, tcx).ty;\\n316:                 if ty.is_union() {\\n317:                     // Different fields of a union, we are basically stuck.\\n318:                     debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: STUCK-UNION\\\");\\n319:                     Overlap::Arbitrary\\n320:                 } else {\\n321:                     // Different fields of a struct (`a.x` vs. `a.y`). Disjoint!\\n322:                     debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-FIELD\\\");\\n323:                     Overlap::Disjoint\\n324:                 }\\n325:             }\\n326:         }\\n327:         (ProjectionElem::Downcast(_, v1), ProjectionElem::Downcast(_, v2)) => {\\n328:             // different variants are treated as having disjoint fields,\\n329:             // even if they occupy the same \\\"space\\\", because it's\\n330:             // impossible for 2 variants of the same enum to exist\\n331:             // (and therefore, to be borrowed) at the same time.\\n332:             //\\n333:             // Note that this is different from unions - we *do* allow\\n334:             // this code to compile:\\n335:             //\\n336:             // ```\\n337:             // fn foo(x: &mut Result<i32, i32>) {\\n338:             //     let mut v = None;\\n339:             //     if let Ok(ref mut a) = *x {\\n340:             //         v = Some(a);\\n341:             //     }\\n342:             //     // here, you would *think* that the\\n343:             //     // *entirety* of `x` would be borrowed,\\n344:             //     // but in fact only the `Ok` variant is,\\n345:             //     // so the `Err` variant is *entirely free*:\\n346:             //     if let Err(ref mut a) = *x {\\n347:             //         v = Some(a);\\n348:             //     }\\n349:             //     drop(v);\\n350:             // }\\n351:             // ```\\n352:             if v1 == v2 {\\n353:                 debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-OR-EQ-FIELD\\\");\\n354:                 Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint\\n355:             } else {\\n356:                 debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-FIELD\\\");\\n357:                 Overlap::Disjoint\\n358:             }\\n359:         }\\n360:         (\\n361:             ProjectionElem::Index(..),\\n362:             ProjectionElem::Index(..)\\n363:             | ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { .. }\\n364:             | ProjectionElem::Subslice { .. },\\n365:         )\\n366:         | (\\n367:             ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { .. } | ProjectionElem::Subslice { .. },\\n368:             ProjectionElem::Index(..),\\n369:         ) => {\\n370:             // Array indexes (`a[0]` vs. `a[i]`). These can either be disjoint\\n371:             // (if the indexes differ) or equal (if they are the same).\\n372:             match bias {\\n373:                 PlaceConflictBias::Overlap => {\\n374:                     // If we are biased towards overlapping, then this is the recursive\\n375:                     // case that gives \\\"equal *or* disjoint\\\" its meaning.\\n376:                     debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-OR-EQ-ARRAY-INDEX\\\");\\n377:                     Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint\\n378:                 }\\n379:                 PlaceConflictBias::NoOverlap => {\\n380:                     // If we are biased towards no overlapping, then this is disjoint.\\n381:                     debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-ARRAY-INDEX\\\");\\n382:                     Overlap::Disjoint\\n383:                 }\\n384:             }\\n385:         }\\n386:         (\\n387:             ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex
